            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Altuve’s short stature and free-swinging approach make him an easy player to root for, but it doesn’t necessarily make him a strong fantasy option. There’s some upside here, however. Altuve is only 21-years-old, has hit for strong averages over his career, and displays speed on the base-paths. Due to his hacktastic approach, his value will likely be very dependent on his BABIP next season. A middle infielder capable of hitting .290 with 20+ steals has value. A middle infielder that hits .250 with no plate discipline, not so much. (Chris Cwik)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Altuve shouldn’t be relied on as a starter in mixed leagues, but he’s shown enough skill to be a late-round sleeper or an injury replacement.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>In a year during which Alcides Escobar hits .291/.331/.390 with five home runs and everyone raves about his offensive improvement, it makes a bit more sense than Jose Altuve can become a minor celebrity by hitting .290/.340/.399 with a Bonds-ian seven dongs. Snarkiness aside, harping on Altuve's power (or the lack thereof) does not really get at the heart of his game, especially for fantasy purposes. As long as he can get on base, he can take advantage of his speed, and players capable of 30 steals a season are nothing to sneeze at in fantasy. Whether Altuve can maintain that .340 on-base percentage is an open question. Despite a below-average walk rate, Altuve is not a total hacker, and does have a very high contact rate. He will need it, because although he will only be 23 next season, his frame does not leave much to build on as far as power development goes. Altuve is draftable as a starter in most leagues, and definitely in those in which steals are a category. (Matt Klaassen)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Jose Altuve may have received undue attention in 2012 because of his size, but in reality he has enough speed to be very playable and maybe even very good fantasy starter in 2013.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>While miniature second baseman Jose Altuve isn’t much of a real-life player yet, the cute little guy is a solid fantasy option. At just 22 years of age in 2012, Altuve stole 30 bags, scored 80 runs, and hit .290 with an above-average on-base percentage, making him one of the top pivots in all of fantasy land. In 2013, Altuve was much less cuddly, but one of his issues stemmed from a lack of production around him in Houston’s lineup. Altuve still hit .283 and stole 35 bases, but he only crossed home 64 times, and his OBP dropped below the league average. With a continuation of a paltry offense around him, Altuve is going to be a fringe starter in standard leagues. If you’re at the end of your draft and realize you need steals, draft Altuve, but his overall value isn’t going to be as high as other second baseman when analyzed in a vacuum. (Zach Sanders)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Jose Altuve’s 2012 breakout didn’t carry over into 2013, and now he looks like a fringe option in standard leagues. Draft him later if you need steals, but don’t expect an all-around contribution.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Jose Altuve was incredible in 2014, ending the year as the league’s third best fantasy player while hitting just seven homers. He hit .341 while stealing 56 bags, and an improved Astros offense allowed him to cross home 85 times. While Altuve may now be the league’s greatest contact hitter, it remains to be seen whether his .341 average is close to repeatable -- the right-hander hit between .276 and .290 in his three previous seasons -- and that average will drive a good deal of his value. Altuve doesn’t walk much, so he’ll need to hit for a high average to get on base enough to steal bags and score runs. When Altuve was hitting below .300, he was still worth $8-$12 in standard leagues, but a .341 hitting Altuve is worth upwards of $35. Odds are Altuve will fall somewhere in between his 2013 and 2014 numbers, making him worthy of being taken by the end of the second round. If you’re in a league that utilizes an extra middle infielder, consider Altuve at the end of the first or early in the second. (Zach Sanders)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Altuve was one of fantasy baseball’s top five players last year, but odds are he won’t repeat. Just 25 years old, Altuve should be off the board in the second round even with regression factored in.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>In 2015, Jose Altuve led the American League in hits and steals for the second straight year. It should be noted, however, that he also led the league in caught stealing in 2015. He had a 75% success rate in last season, all together. However, he did manage to lean into a lot of home runs (at least for him), totaling 15 dingers in his 2015 campaign. His overall batting line wasn't as good as it was in 2014, but it was still quite solid (120 vs. a 134 weighted runs created plus). He's a cornerstone in Houston, and barely misses time, so he'll certainly get his chances. His 2014 season was probably a bit of an aberration, but a season similar to 2015 certainly seems like a reasonable assumption. Expect the power and speed numbers to repeat from last season, for the most part, though Altuve will only be entering his age-26 season, so another power spike is certainly possible. Second base is still fairly shallow, so Altuve will most certainly be gone by the third round. (David Temple)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Altuve is a very good player at a premium position. While his 2014 speed numbers and 2015 power numbers are unlikely to come together like Voltron to produce a fantasy powerhouse, he's still a great fantasy player that should be gone by the third round.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Who knew you could pack so much punch into a compact 5'7, 170 pound body?! Not only did Altuve prove that his 2015 power spike was no fluke, he actually boosted that power to even greater heights, en route to notching his first 20/30 campaign. It's now officially official -- Altuve does it all. He even easily set a new career high in walk rate and struck out less than 10% of the time for the third straight season. His second power surge was driven by an added two miles per hour of average fly ball and line drive exit velocity. But is this sustainable? It's hard to believe that he's still just 26 years old. His age suggests that home runs in the teens, at the very least, are here to stay. And until he slows down the running game, he remains an easy first rounder. (<a href="http://www.projectingx.com/" target="_blank">Mike Podhorzer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Altuve has gone from strong three category contributor, to three and a half category star, to five category fantasy monster...and he's still only 26 years old! Obviously, odds are high that he suffers some regression across the board after what might prove to be his career year, but he's still easily a first round pick and as safe a choice as one could hope for.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>
